Number of Troops Not Withdrawn　Regarding the withdrawal of Japanese troops, according to Mr. Okazaki, the army has already withdrawn. There are approximately 40 Marines at the Wusong Huafeng Mill. The number of Marines at the Toyota Mill, the Gong Da Mill, and the Tongwen Academy is roughly the same. Although the exact number of those still remaining in Shanghai is unknown, it is estimated to be over 2,500.

Deployment Removed　Regarding the deployment of Japanese troops and the erection of barbed wire west of Sajing Port at 5:30 PM the day before yesterday, after receiving a report from the Third Section of the Fifth District, the Management Committee notified our member of the Joint Committee, requesting that the matter be brought up in the Joint Committee. At that time, Commissioners Yu Hongjun and Wen Yingxing considered the matter briefly and decided to first send a letter to the chairman of the Joint Committee, and then convene a meeting if necessary. However, according to a report from the Public Security Bureau yesterday morning, the barbed wire at the Hu Jia Mu Bridge and the Xiangyan Bridge had been removed, and the searches of pedestrians had also been canceled. Therefore, Commissioners Yu and others immediately stopped notifying the Joint Committee. It was also reported that the Japanese troops only erected barbed wire and searched pedestrians the day before yesterday, and did not deploy positions.

Although the deployment was removed yesterday, occasional stray soldiers are still being spotted.

Japanese Soldiers Still Spotted Yesterday 149

Barbed Wire at Hu Jia Mu Bridge Removed After Negotiations

Public Security Bureau Says No Accidents Expected

In the area west of Sajing Port in East Shanghai, Japanese soldiers have been spotted recently, checking pedestrians, deploying positions, and setting up barbed wire, causing considerable alarm among nearby residents. Japanese soldiers were still traveling there yesterday, but according to the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, this has been happening sporadically for days and no accidents are expected. The barbed wire at the Hu Jia Mu Bridge was removed yesterday morning. The news obtained yesterday is recorded below:

Japanese Soldiers Still Traveling　Japanese Army and Navy battle troops went to the area west of Sajing Bridge, Xiangyan Bridge, and Hu Jia Mu Bridge the night before last and last night for extensive searches. At 11:00 AM yesterday, they patrolled the area again, with about thirty to forty people, all fully armed, patrolling in armored vehicles, creating a serious situation. They left after about an hour.

Barbed Wire Removed　The barbed wire installed by the Japanese army at the Hu Jia Mu Bridge the day before yesterday was several feet long, with only a narrow pedestrian walkway in the middle, barely wide enough for one person to pass through. Those crossing the bridge had to be searched. After the barbed wire was installed, the Municipal Public Security Bureau, upon receiving a report, forwarded it to the Management Committee, requesting that Mr. Yu Hongjun, our member of the Joint Committee, go and negotiate with the Japanese side, stating that this matter could easily cause misunderstandings and should be removed. The Japanese side immediately ordered the Marines to remove it yesterday morning. By the afternoon, the Hu Jia Mu Bridge was able to be passed without obstruction.

Reasons for Japanese Military Patrols　The sudden appearance of Japanese soldiers west of Sajing Port this time has caused considerable suspicion in the outside world. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency has learned that the reason is that traitors are hiding in the area west of Sajing Port, opening gambling dens and "swallow nests." There are now more than a dozen large and small gambling dens in the area. Fearing that they would be discovered by the police, they asked the Japanese army to maintain strict guard.

Eastern District Still Peaceful　Yesterday afternoon, a reporter went to the area west of Sajing Port and Tiantong Road, Hu Jia Mu Bridge, and Xiangyan Bridge in the Eastern District and saw that the Japanese soldiers had retreated. The situation in the area was still peaceful, but there were few pedestrians. This area is originally a desolate place. Linping Road, Hongzhen, and Xingang have been taken over by our side, so they are quite lively and many shops are open as usual. However, there is still a curfew at night.

Statement from the Public Security Bureau　Yesterday morning, a reporter from the New Voice News Agency interviewed Gong Xikui, the Inspector General of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, about the situation in East Shanghai. According to him, the situation there is not as serious as reported. The area is as normal. There have been many rumors in Zhabei in recent days, causing anxiety among the people. He advised the outside world not to believe them lightly. Later,

he visited Wu Yanxun, the chief of the Third Section of the Fifth District, which has jurisdiction over East Shanghai. According to him, the area patrolled by the Japanese soldiers is the area that our side has not yet taken over. The Third Section of the Fifth District has six police stations: Hongzhen, Xingang Road, Linping Road, Jixiang Road, Oujia Road, and Pingmin Village. Currently, Hongzhen, Xingang Road, and Linping Road have been recovered, but the rest have not yet been recovered. Therefore, the Japanese soldiers spotted in recent days have been in the unrecovered area. It is estimated that they are sent out by the Japanese garrison team in the Fourth District (i.e., Zhabei District). However, they are only patrolling and not permanently deploying positions. They leave after staying for some time and there are no conflicts. The area is still quite peaceful.

Strike by Telephone Workers in the Concession

The Situation Is Becoming More Serious 152

Because the Company Did Not Provide a Concrete Reply Yesterday Morning

And Arrested Four Worker Representatives

Meeting at the Public Sports Ground Also Failed

After the strike by the telephone company workers in the Concession, the company still did not provide a concrete reply to the new conditions proposed by the workers yesterday. The representatives were arrested by the police, the Fujian Road branch was temporarily placed under martial law, and the meeting of workers at the Public Sports Ground was also stopped by the Public Security Bureau. The strike situation is becoming more serious. Details of the various events are recorded below:

Temporary Martial Law　The Public Concession Police, having received reports that the striking telephone company workers had gathered at the Fujian Road telephone branch at 7:00 AM on the 10th, under the orders of the Strike Committee, dispatched over a hundred Chinese and foreign armed detectives to temporarily impose martial law at 6:30 AM yesterday morning. They advised pedestrians standing by the roadside to disperse. By around 7:00 AM, striking workers came in groups of three or five and stood by the roadside waiting for news of the company's reply. By around 9:00 AM, over a thousand people had gathered, causing traffic to be blocked. The detectives tried to restore traffic, but the striking workers and onlookers remained.

Negotiations Ineffective　By 10:10 AM, all the workers, seeing that the company had not yet come out to reply to the conditions they had proposed, sent four representatives, Ye Gongzhao, Zheng Luojie, Xu Shijie, and Pan Dingquan, to the Fujian Road telephone branch to request an audience with the manager. They were met by the engineer Wilson, who told the representatives that the conditions proposed by the workers were in Chinese and were currently being translated into English, but the translation had not yet been completed, so a reply could not be given temporarily. A reply would be given after the translation was completed. The representatives believed that the company was not sincere in accepting the conditions and left together.

Representatives Arrested　After the representatives left, they announced the outcome of the negotiations to the workers waiting for news by the roadside. All the workers were very angry and shouted slogans such as "Oppose the company firing workers!", "We will not resume work until we achieve our goals!", "Support the Strike Committee!", which caused some disorder. The Chinese and foreign detectives immediately intervened and

arrested all the worker representatives Ye Gongzhao, workers Wan Ruichun, Zhang Rongsheng, and Zhu Ziwun, and dispersed the workers standing by the roadside.

Meeting Stopped　After all the striking workers were dispersed by the police, they immediately followed the Strike Committee's temporary urgent order and went to the Public Sports Ground in Ximen to hold a general meeting to discuss the next steps. By around 11:00 AM, over 400 workers had gathered at the Public Sports Ground and distributed the second declaration. When the meeting was about to begin, the Second Police Station of the Municipal Public Security Bureau sent police officers to inquire, claiming that the meeting had not been permitted by the Public Security Bureau, the Social Affairs Bureau, or the Municipal Party Headquarters, and advised them to stop. After the workers repeatedly negotiated with the police officers without success, the Second Police Station sent more police officers to disperse them at around 12:00 PM because the workers had not dispersed. The workers had no choice but to disperse.

Reception for Reporters　The Strike Committee sent letters to various newspapers and news agencies yesterday morning, saying, "We are writing to inform you that, in order to allow all sectors to understand the truth of the strike, the workers have decided to host reporters from various newspapers at 10:00 AM on the 10th at the Huzhongtian Teahouse on Fujian Road. We hope that your newspaper will send someone to participate on time." At 10:00 AM, reporters from various newspapers and news agencies went there,

just as the workers were shouting slogans. Because the representatives were arrested, the reception for reporters was postponed.

Workers' Attitude　The Strike Committee told reporters yesterday about the truth of the strike, saying that the motive of this strike is first to seek self-protection and second to oppose the unreasonable oppression of capitalists. The workers are acting entirely on their own and will not be disunited by the company's rumors.

The company has issued statements and announcements to try to undermine the workers, but this has only made the workers even more angry. The company is now showing no sincerity in the conditions proposed by the workers and is making excuses to delay. But all our workers will continue to strike until we achieve our goals. Our contact point with all sectors is the Tongshang Hotel on Avenue Road, the Shanghai Telephone Workers Strike Committee Contact Point.

Mayor Wu Hosted a Banquet for the Press Yesterday 157

Mayor Wu Tiecheng believes that the affairs of Shanghai have come to an end, so yesterday he

made time to host a banquet at the Hua'an Building for reporters from various newspapers and news agencies. At 1:00 PM, guests and hosts gathered. Mr. Wu, accompanied by Yu Hongjun, Secretary-General of the Municipal Government, Chen Kecheng, Director of Propaganda, and Chen Xunshe, and others hosted the banquet. During the banquet, Mayor Wu stood up and delivered a speech, saying that since taking office, unfortunately, the war broke out, and he had to deal with it day and night, without any time to get together with everyone, which he had always regretted. Now that the affairs of Shanghai have come to an end, and his responsibilities are lighter, he has prepared some dishes today to have a brief chat with everyone. There are many old friends in the audience today, and also many new acquaintances. It is truly a pleasure to have a good chat on this occasion. During this war, fortunately, local people and journalists made every effort to cooperate and assist, which made it easier to cope with. He is especially grateful for this. In the future, the post-war recovery and reconstruction of the area will depend even more on everyone's assistance. He deeply hopes that everyone will lend a helping hand, which is what he further hopes for.

Lottery Redemption of Seven Types of Public Bonds 159

Total Redemption of 1,474,000 Yuan

Payment Period for the Second and Fourth Quarter Treasury Bills is After the 20th and Before the End of the Month

The Ministry of Finance's sixth redemption of the Austrian Indemnity Secured Second and Fourth Quarter Treasury Bills, the tenth redemption of the 6% Public Bonds of the Republic of China (1918), the tenth redemption of the Public Bonds of the Republic of China (1925), the seventh redemption of the National Government Ministry of Finance Military Bonds, the ninth redemption of the Post-War Short-Term Public Bonds, the eighth redemption of the Famine Relief Public Bonds (1919), and the sixth redemption of the Customs Revenue Public Bonds (1930) were all held at the Bank Association at No. 4 Hong Kong Road at 10:00 AM yesterday. Details of each item are recorded below.

Representatives Present　Yesterday, the auditors from the Supervisory Council of the Ministry of Audit, Yin Gongwu, Fang Jiaobo from the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, Fan Jietang from the National Debt Fund Management Committee, Sun Jingxi from the Bank Association, Pei Yunqing from the Money Trade Association, Li Shouqing from the Second Branch of the High Court, Li Tisheng from the Central Bank, Zhu Qizhen from the Bank of China, Jin Wenshen from the Bank of Communications, Huang Guoen, Lu Shutang, He Xiaoqing, and Liang Yaoshou from the Management Committee, Chen Shaochao, You

Page 14

Dun, Lu Zhixing, and Chen Jian, clerks Huang Qizong, Xu Huang, Huang Meizhao, receptionists Wang Shulin, He Yaoqing, Zheng Luojian, Ji Juncai, Luo Peide, Xu Ruifang from the Jianghai Customs General Tax Office, Xue Jingren from the Xingye Bank, Luo Jingxian from the City Bank, and over forty other people were present.

Chairman's Report　Zheng Ye, Director of the Public Debt Department of the Ministry of Finance, reported that today is the date for the lottery redemption of seven types of bonds, including the Austrian Indemnity Secured Second and Fourth Quarter Treasury Bills. He was grateful for everyone's presence and would briefly report on the situation of each type of bond. (1) The Austrian Indemnity Secured Second and Fourth Quarter Treasury Bills were issued in 1926 for a total of 2.4 million yuan. They have already been redeemed five times. This is the sixth

redemption. Each winning ticket will be redeemed for 24,000 silver yuan. (2) The 6% Public Bonds of the Republic of China (1918) were issued for a total of 45 million yuan. They have already been redeemed nine times. This is the tenth redemption. Each winning ticket will be redeemed for 450,000 silver yuan. (3) The Public Bonds of the Republic of China (1925) were issued for a total of 15 million yuan. They have already been redeemed nine times. This is the tenth redemption. Each winning ticket will be redeemed for 150,000 silver yuan. (4) The National Government Ministry of Finance Military Bonds were issued in 1928 for a total of 10 million yuan. They have already been redeemed six times. This is the seventh redemption. Each winning ticket will be redeemed for 100,000 silver yuan. (5) The National Government Ministry of Finance Post-War Short-Term Public Bonds were issued in 1928 for a total of 40 million yuan. They have already been redeemed eight times. This is the ninth redemption. Each winning ticket will be redeemed for 400,000 silver yuan. (6) The Famine Relief Public Bonds (1929) were issued for a total of 10 million yuan. They have already been redeemed seven times. This

is the eighth redemption. Each winning ticket will be redeemed for 100,000 silver yuan. (7) The Customs Revenue Public Bonds (1930) were issued for a total of 20 million yuan. They have already been redeemed five times. This is the sixth redemption. Each winning ticket will be redeemed for 200,000 silver yuan. All the winning bond tickets, except for the Austrian Indemnity Secured Second and Fourth Quarter Treasury Bills, which are scheduled to be paid starting June 20th, all other six types of bond tickets are scheduled to be paid starting June 30th. All the winning bonds should be paid by the Central, China, and Transportation Banks, together with the interest on each bond, upon maturity. Please inspect the winning ticket and the winning ticket register for execution of the lottery.

Winning Numbers　After the supervisors inspected the winning tickets and the winning ticket register, the lottery drawer executed the lottery. The winning numbers are recorded below. (1) One Austrian Indemnity Secured Second and Fourth Quarter Treasury Bill, "No. 72." (2) One 6% Public Bond of the Republic of China (1918), "No. 68." (3) One Public Bond of the Republic of China (1925), "No. 64." (4) One National Government Ministry of Finance Military Bond, "No. 66." (5) One National Government Ministry of Finance Post-War Short-Term Public Bond, "No. 95." (6) One Famine Relief Public Bond (1929), "No. 18." (7) One Customs Revenue Public Bond (1930), "No. 04." A total of 1,474,000 yuan will be redeemed.

Ministry of Finance Announcement　For announcement, the sixth redemption of the Austrian Indemnity Secured Second and Fourth Quarter Treasury Bills, the tenth redemption of the 6% Public Bonds of the Republic of China (1918), the tenth redemption of the Public Bonds of the Republic of China (1925), the seventh redemption of the National Government Ministry of Finance Military Bonds, the ninth redemption of the Post-War Short-Term Public Bonds, the eighth redemption of the Famine Relief Public Bonds (1919), and the sixth redemption of the Customs Revenue Public Bonds (1930) were all executed at the Shanghai Banking Association on June 10th. All holders of the above-mentioned bonds whose last two digits of the bond face number are the same as the winning numbers of the corresponding bonds listed in the attached table are the winning bonds for this redemption. All the principal that should be redeemed,

the Austrian Indemnity Secured Second and Fourth Quarter Treasury Bills, is scheduled for June 20th, and the remaining six types of public bonds are scheduled for June 30th, to be paid by the Central, China, and Transportation Banks, with a three-year period, and no further payments will be made after the period expires.

In addition to sending separate letters to comply, we are announcing this so that everyone will be informed. June 10th, 21st year of the Republic of China, Song Ziwen, Minister of Finance.

Industrial and Commercial Rehabilitation Association of Disaster Areas

Yesterday's Collective Discussion on Reconstruction Plan 160

Establishing a Special Committee to Design and Implement

The Disaster Area Industry and Commerce Reconstruction Association, a joint organization of various industries in the disaster area of this city, held its first committee meeting yesterday at 3 PM to discuss the reconstruction plan. It was decided to send letters to various groups to solicit opinions and to establish a special committee. The details are recorded below:

Committee Meeting: The first committee meeting was held at 49 Hankou Road yesterday at 3 PM. More than ten people attended, including Qiu Liangyu, Ye Jiaxing, Zhong Yibo, Xie Zhongle, Cheng Guichu, Pan Xusheng, Hu Yuantang, Cai Qiajun, Jin Wenxiang, Zhou Shizhang, and Yuan Hongjun. Ye Jiaxing chaired the meeting, and Sun Mingqi recorded the minutes. The following important matters were resolved: (1) Discussing the association's charter: it was resolved to amend and approve it (the charter is attached below). (2) Electing standing committee members: it was resolved to elect Zhang Yuchi, Ye Jiaxing, Zhong Yibo, Zhang Dalian, Gan Zheluo, Xie Zhongle, and Pan Xusheng as standing committee members. (3) Electing heads of various departments: it was resolved that Hu Yuantang and Li Ruzhang would be in charge of general affairs; Wu Zhongyi and Jin Wenxiang would be in charge of finance; Cai Qiaqun and Zhou Xingqiong would be in charge of investigation; and Cheng Guichu and Yuan Hongjun would be in charge of statistics. (4) Discussing how to raise funds for the association: it was resolved to entrust the standing committee and the finance department to formulate fundraising methods and then submit them to the meeting for discussion. (5) Discussing the association's request to the national government for relief: it was resolved that the secretary would draft the document. (6) Secretary-General of the Association: it was resolved to hire Sun Mingqi and Su Guangfen. (7) Discussing the association's request to the municipal government for tax exemption: it was resolved to have the secretary draft the document. (8) Discussing how to revive the disaster-stricken industries and businesses in the city: it was resolved that (A) letters would be sent to various industrial and commercial groups to solicit opinions on the reconstruction of the disaster area; (B) the standing committee would be responsible for formulating a list and organizing a special committee to design and implement the plan; (C) the investigation department would investigate the amount of losses from the Sanji organs' loss registration office for reference. (9) Yuan Hongjun proposed that the association should send a letter to the Sanji organs' loss registration office to extend the registration period to benefit the disaster-stricken industries and businesses. The resolution was passed. (10) Zhou Shizhang proposed that the association should inquire about the war zone rehabilitation committee's emergency relief of 1.1 million yuan and the emergency relief methods. The resolution was passed. (11) Regarding the association's address: it was resolved that Xie Zhongle, Pan Xusheng, Ye Jiaxing, and Zhong Yibo would contact the municipal chamber of commerce to borrow a place. (12) Regarding the date of the association's committee meeting: it was resolved to hold a meeting every two weeks, on Friday afternoons at 3 PM. (13) Regarding how to formulate the association's rules of procedure and the detailed rules of procedure for each department: it was resolved to entrust the standing committee members and the heads of each department to formulate them.

Simplified Rules Passed: The full text of the simplified rules of the Municipal Disaster Area Industry and Commerce Reconstruction Committee is as follows: Article 1: This association is organized by merchants from various industries in the disaster area of Shanghai, hence the name Shanghai Municipal Disaster Area Industry and Commerce Reconstruction Committee. Article 2: The purpose of this association is to revive industry and commerce in the disaster area. Article 3: This association shall have 21 executive committee members, publicly recommended from among the representatives of various industries. Article 4: This association should have seven standing committee members and four departments: general affairs, finance, investigation, and statistics. Each department should have one director and one deputy director, and the candidates should be mutually elected from among the committee members. Article 5: The executive committee meeting of this association shall be held once every two weeks, and the standing committee meeting shall be held once a week. However, if necessary, it may be convened temporarily. Article 6: In order to gather ideas and expand association affairs, this association may hire leaders of industry and commerce to establish a special committee. Article 7: This association may hire a secretary and a number of staff members as necessary for the conduct of business. Article 8: If this association encounters urgent matters, it may convene a meeting of representatives from various industries with the resolution of the committee. Article 9: The regular expenses of this association shall be subsidized by various industrial and commercial groups. Article 10: The detailed rules of procedure for this association shall be formulated separately. Article 11: These simplified rules shall be implemented upon resolution by the committee meeting, and the same shall apply to amendments.

Passengers to Japan to Be Inspected for Epidemics Starting Today 164

This year, the outbreak of epidemics in this port occurred earlier than in any other year. Therefore, Japan has sent a telegram officially recognizing Shanghai as a port with epidemics. The Japanese mail ship "Shanghai Maru" was even detained and prohibited from sailing due to the discovery of passengers with epidemics. Passengers traveling to Japan starting today will be subject to inspection. Details are as follows: The Shanghai Maru is Detained for Disinfection, Contacted by the Japan Mail Company's Fast Ferry "Shanghai Maru". The last time the "Shanghai Maru" sailed from Shanghai to the East, it carried a large number of passengers. When the ship arrived in Nagasaki, it was discovered that several passengers were critically ill. After examination by medical officers at the port's quarantine station, it was confirmed that they had contracted cholera. The "Shanghai Maru" was immediately detained and not allowed to enter the port. It was immediately moved to an outer port. All the personnel and passengers on board were examined, and the ship was disinfected. The ship was also prohibited from sailing for two weeks. Therefore, the "Shanghai Maru" has not been in Shanghai for many days. It will not resume its regular schedule until the 17th of this month.

Various Shipping Companies Received Telegrams to Comply 165

Shanghai's various Japanese shipping companies received telegrams from their respective headquarters in Japan yesterday stating that cholera has been discovered in Shanghai and it has been officially recognized as a port with epidemics. From June 10th onwards, all passengers traveling from Shanghai to Japan, regardless of which ship they are traveling on, must complete quarantine procedures. A quarantine station has been established in Nagasaki, and many medical officers have been dispatched to specialize in inspecting passengers traveling from Shanghai to Japan. Yesterday, the shipping companies received telegrams and have already complied with epidemic prevention matters.

Quarantine Measures Have Been Stipulated 166

The Japan Mail Company stipulated quarantine measures yesterday. When passengers purchase tickets to Japan, they will be given a copy of the quarantine regulations. After passengers board the ship, the shipowner will issue a wax box and instruct everyone to store their feces in the box. When they arrive at the first port, they will be collected and submitted to the medical officer at the quarantine station for chemical examination. If there is an epidemic, the passenger will be immediately detained and confined to an isolation room, prohibited from landing. If there is no epidemic, they will be allowed to disembark. The announcement is as follows: Due to the discovery of epidemic diseases circulating in Shanghai (according to Japanese quarantine regulations), passengers must prepare their own fecal samples before the ship arrives at the port. Passengers departing from Shanghai must go to the quarantine station upon arrival at the first port and wait for the doctor to examine them with a microscope before being allowed to pass. The expenses for meals, etc., required during the inspection shall be borne by the passengers. After the inspection, if there is still waiting or delay, the meal expenses, etc., shall also be borne by the passengers.

Passengers from North China Also Inspected: Epidemics have also been found among passengers traveling from Tianjin to Japan. It is said that there are more than 50 people who have been examined. At present, various Japanese ships sailing from Tianjin to the East are also implementing quarantine. Other cargo ships that are not carrying passengers but are sailing from Shanghai or Tianjin to the East, their crew members and sailors must also be inspected before landing. At the same time, crew members and sailors on various Japanese ships are prohibited from landing in Shanghai to prevent transmission.

China Travel Service

Inviting the Press to Pay Respects to the War Zone 170

Heroic War Achievements

Desolate Scenery

The China Travel Service at 114 Sichuan Road, in view of the fact that the 19th Route Army's anti-Japanese operations in Shanghai this time brought glory to our nation and were of great significance, has organized a war zone visitation group.

In order to allow citizens to visit the important war relics in Wusong, Jiangwan, and Zhabei districts in the most economical time and at the most economical cost, since the 3rd of this month, the number of visitors to the war zone has been 500 per day. Yesterday, Chen Xiangtao, the president of the company, specially invited the Shanghai press to conduct a half-day inspection. At 1:30 PM, they departed from the front of the head office. More than ten representatives from various newspapers participated, riding in four new-style cars provided by the Liyi Automobile Company, which were stable, fast, and comfortable, and most suitable for observation. Along the way, inspectors from the travel agency, Hu Shiyuan, and Deng Bingquan, the director of the navigation department, accompanied them. They departed from Sichuan Road and went straight to Wusong and Paotaiwan. Along the way, they passed through Hongkou Park, West Sports Association Road, Chizhi University, Xiangyin Road, Xuzhi Company, Fudan University, Jungong Road, Water and Electricity Plant, Junpu Bureau, Yunzaohong, Wusong Town, Seaside Hotel, Meteorological Station, and Radio Station. After arriving at Paotaiwan, they visited the relics of the fort. More than ten cannons were all destroyed by the enemy army. The foundations of the fort were bombarded by enemy aircraft and artillery and were all shattered. Huge rocks were thrown dozens of feet away. Those who saw this situation could not help but sigh with sorrow. They paid respects at the fort, took photos for commemoration, and left Wusong at 3:45 PM.

They still went from Jungong Road to Xiangyin Road and got off the bus at the Xuzhi Company to rest briefly and have some snacks. They also visited the disinfection room and cattle barn, etc. The equipment was complete and the products were excellent. It was the leader of large-scale dairy farms run by the Chinese. At around 5 o'clock, they returned to Shanghai via Jiangwan Road. They passed through Tengpei Road, West Sports Association Road, Tongji Road, Baziqiao, Qingyun Road, Tiantong'an Railway Station, Japanese Naval Headquarters, North Sichuan Road, Dongbaoxing Road, Baoshan Road, Commercial Press, Oriental Library, and North Railway Station, and returned to the travel agency. What they saw along the way was broken walls and scorched earth, a scene of desolation. Especially the areas around Baziqiao and Baoshan Road suffered even more severely. The fierceness of the 19th Route Army's resistance at that time can be imagined. The war zone visitation group departs twice a day, the first shift at 8:30 AM, and the second shift at 1:30 PM. The fare is two yuan and two jiao per person, and the round trip takes about four and a half hours. Those who want to visit the war zone ruins with economical time should consider this route as the most suitable.

Municipal Federation of Trade Unions Retains the 19th Route Army 173

Reply from the Military Affairs Commission

The Shanghai Municipal Federation of Trade Unions' affiliated dock workers' consolidation association, the dock workers' union in districts 1 and 2, the ink makers' union, the tea industry union, the silk reeling industry unions in districts 1, 3, 4, and 6, the Cantonese steamship woodworking union, the umbrella union, the western district yarn factory, the Xihe yarn factory union, and 27 other unions in contact with various circles in Suzhou, Wuxi, and Changzhou went to Beijing to retain the 19th Route Army and submitted petitions to various authorities. Yesterday, they received a reply from the Military Affairs Commission, which read: Regarding the submitted petition requesting that the authorities conform to public opinion,

approve the withdrawal of the order and maintain the original defense, consolidate Shanghai and Nanjing, the petition and the face-to-face request from the representatives to retain the troops, all are noted. The representatives love their hometowns and prepare for contingencies, which is only right. This commission takes into consideration the overall situation and weighs the importance,

and should respond urgently to what is urgent and prioritize what is important. Now that all the bandit suppression plans have been decided, it is not appropriate to disrupt the overall situation. Shanghai and Nanjing have other military and police stationed there, so the request should not be discussed. This is approved by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, Republic of China, June 8, 1932.

The Da Mei Wanbao reports that the U.S. transport ship "Chaumont," carrying the Fourth Marine Regiment and other naval units for a change of station, 254 officers and soldiers, arrived in Shanghai last night (9th). Dunluop Injured in Car Accident 176

Skull Fractured, Unconscious

The North-China Daily News reports that Dunluop, the Chinese Affairs Vice-Consul of the British Consulate-General, was traveling with a friend in his own car to the Paris Grand Theatre on Wednesday night. Because he was not familiar with the address of the theatre, he drove to the front of the Guanghua Cinema on Avenue Edward VII, thinking it was Paris. He stopped the car on the opposite side of the road. Dunluop got out of the car, walked across the road, and inquired. He found out that it was not the right place and was about to return to the car. Unexpectedly, as soon as he left the sidewalk, he was hit by a car on duty, his skull fractured, and he lost consciousness. His friend took him to the Hong'en Hospital, where three doctors performed a hemostasis operation on him. After several hours, the bleeding stopped, but his condition was still extremely dangerous. If there are no changes within 48 hours, there is hope for recovery. Dunluop has been working at the British Consulate-General in this port for two years. Before that, he worked at the British Legation in Beijing for two years, it is said.

The Two Sheng Family Lawsuits 184

Litigation Unceasing, All for Money

Zhuang Family Will Has Witnesses

Wang Sheng Rong Case 185

Wang Sheng Rong is married to a Mr. Wang from Suzhou and is the granddaughter of Sheng Yu Zhai, a prominent official from the previous Qing dynasty, the biological daughter of Sheng Kui Chen, and the adopted daughter of Sheng Ai Chen. After Ai Chen's death, Yu You, the son of Ze Chen, was adopted as his heir. After Yu Zhai's death, Wang Sheng Rong, based on the equal rights of children law, filed a lawsuit with the First Special District Court against Yu You to equally divide the inheritance. Subsequently, due to identity issues, the case was to be determined by the High Court. In the 16th year of the Republic, Yu Zhai's wife, Zhuang, also passed away, leaving a will distributing 75,000 yuan to Ai Chen's name (i.e., Yu You inherited). Therefore, the property was not equally divided with Wang Sheng Rong. For this reason, she filed another lawsuit with the First Special District Court to equally divide 37,500 yuan. Yesterday was the date for the review, and Judge Li Hu presided over the hearing in the Seventh Civil Court. First, Wang Sheng Rong provided a detailed account of her identity, stating:

When Grandpa Yu Zhai was alive, he was very fond of me and I attended to him closely, sharing his meals and rest. After Yu Zhai's death, I continued to rely on my grandmother Zhuang, and Ai Chen also loved me very much. Moreover, Wang Sheng Rong's biological father had passed away early, so Ai Chen adopted me as his daughter, treating me as his own. When Ai Chen was on his deathbed, I personally attended to his medicine, and after his death, I wore mourning attire. Everything a filial child should do, I did to the fullest. One week after Ai Chen's death, my grandmother Zhuang established Yu You as Ai Chen's heir. This was because Ai Chen's wife had passed away early and he never remarried, and later only had a concubine as his wife, but she had no children either. After her grandmother Zhuang passed away, she divided 75,000 yuan of her estate to Ai Chen's heir, Yu You. Because Ai Chen had already adopted Wang Sheng Rong as his daughter, she has the right to request half of it. As for why I also sued Sheng Ze Chen, it is because Yu You's property is currently entirely managed by him. The defendant did not appear, and lawyer Jiang Bao Li represented him, stating that this case is similar to the previous lawsuit to equally divide Yu Zhai's inheritance. The only difference is that

it involves the inheritance of the grandmother instead of the grandfather. Now that the previous case has been suspended for deliberation due to Wang Sheng Rong's identity issue, and she is still awaiting a clarification of her identity in the High Court, it seems that the proceedings in this case should also be suspended to avoid conflicting judgments in the future. The plaintiff's lawyer, Li Zu Yu, then rose to object, stating that when Wang Sheng Rong got married, Ai Chen handled everything as if she were his own daughter, and there are as many as sixteen pieces of evidence to prove her adoption. Because witnesses still need to be summoned, the hearing was rescheduled for a later date.

Shao Yun Peng Case 186

Shao Yun Peng, Yun Zhi, Yun Jun, Yun Qi, Yun Lin, and Yun Xiang are born to Zhi Hui, the biological daughter of Sheng Gong Bao from the previous Qing dynasty. In the 16th year of the Republic, Gong Bao's wife, Zhuang, passed away, leaving a large inheritance. It was not until November 2nd of last year that the will was discovered, stating that the fourth, fifth, sixth, and eighth daughters should each receive 10,000 yuan. A Mr. Lin Feng Wen, with the qualification of a maternal grandson, requested the First Special District Court, on the grounds that women have inheritance rights, to equally divide the inheritance as the daughter of Gong Bao, and accused Sheng Ze Cheng, Pan Chen, Jian Chen, Yu Chang, Yu You, Guan Yi, Fang Yi, Ai Yi, and Jing Yi of embezzlement. The Sheng family therefore filed a counterclaim for false accusation, and the case was dismissed. Therefore, the authenticity of the will became an issue. This will was only discovered several years after Zhuang's death, raising many doubts. For this reason, Shao Yun Peng and others also commissioned lawyer Dong Yu to file a complaint with the First Special District Court, accusing the Sheng family brothers and sisters of forging the will and embezzling the inheritance. This case had been heard, but the preliminary trial judge recused himself for some reason. Yesterday, Judge Shen Bing Rong continued the trial. The most important point in this case is whether the will is genuine, when it was made, and how it was discovered. The Sheng family brothers and sisters then presented Shen Yi Qing, who wrote the will, and Li Pu Cheng and Zhuang Feng Ying, who were present at the time, as witnesses. Shen Yi Qing testified that he was the person who drafted and transcribed the will. It was written after Zhuang's sixtieth birthday. Because Zhuang felt that lawsuits had arisen after the death of Gong Bao's concubine, she wrote the will to avoid disputes after her death and to resolve lawsuits. When it was written, Li Pu Cheng and Zhuang Feng Ying were present. It was after dinner, and Zhuang dictated while Shen Yi Qing drafted and then transcribed it. After Zhuang read it, she stamped it with her seal. However, Zhuang specifically instructed that the will must not be made known to her children and grandchildren until after her death and funeral arrangements were completed. It must be kept secret during her lifetime. When questioned, Li Pu Cheng and Zhuang Feng Ying gave similar testimony. However, Judge Shen said to the witnesses, "It is fortunate that this will was discovered last year. If it had been unfortunately lost forever, would Zhuang's painstaking efforts have been in vain? Therefore, the three people who were present when the will was written did not announce it immediately after Zhuang's death. Did they also fail Zhuang's intentions on that day?" The three witnesses said, "If this will had been unfortunately lost, we would have definitely mentioned Zhuang's intentions when the property was divided." Because the plaintiff mistakenly believed that the judge had recused himself from the hearing, or perhaps the hearing had been changed, the plaintiffs did not appear in court. The court ordered the hearing to be rescheduled to summon them again.

The Moustache Issue of "Night Blooming Flower" 196

One of the Bandits in a Kidnapping Case

Lawyer Raises a Clever Argument

Hu Yun Qing, a famous gangster nicknamed "Night Blooming Flower" from Changzhou, was involved in a case where Cai Fu Lin, a comprador for the British American Tobacco Company, was kidnapped by bandits years ago and released after his family paid a large ransom. After the case was investigated and punished, he fled to other places to hide. Recently, he was discovered by detectives from the Jiangyin Public Security Bureau at the Tian Xian Tea Garden in the county. They notified the General Inspectorate of the Public Concession, and Chief Detective Lu Lian Kui sent Detective Feng Zhi Ming to Cheng to bring him to Shanghai. He was handed over to the First Special District Court. After interrogation, he admitted that he had received 1,000 yuan of the ransom money. Yesterday morning, Judge Feng Shi De proposed to continue the trial. Although the defendant Hu Yun Qing was repeatedly questioned by Judge Feng, he only insisted that he was innocent and had nothing else to say. When questioned again, he overturned his previous admission in court that he had received 1,000 yuan of the ransom money. His lawyer then made a humorous request, stating that the victim Cai Fu Lin and his wife had previously testified that the bandit who contacted them did not have a moustache, but the defendant's lips now have a mustache. Therefore, to examine his face, it would be best to allow the defendant to shave off his beard and call Cai's wife to court again to identify him, in order to be prudent. Originally, to identify a face, it must be white and without a beard in order to recognize the true face of Mount Lu. Therefore, the defendant's beard is of great importance and should be noted. For a moment, the audience, hearing the lawyer's clever argument, laughed. However, Judge Feng said that even if the defendant has a beard, his face would not be completely changed by the beard. The request to shave his beard is unnecessary, so he did not approve the request and immediately ordered the debate to begin. The police lawyer Wang Yao Tang and the defendant's three defense lawyers then debated in turn. It was already past noon. Judge Feng ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody and await sentencing at a later date.

Stealing Blank Checks from a Shop 197

Filling Out 300 Yuan and Cashing It

Zhao A Qiao from Shaoxing used to work as a shop assistant at Cun Ji Ren Yang Qian Zhuang at No. 33 Huangpu Road. He quit during the war and became unemployed. His courtyard was empty and he could not maintain his livelihood. On the 16th of last month at about 6 p.m., he sneaked into the shop's accounting room and stole a bankbook and a blank check for 300 yuan, filled it out, and cashed it at a bank on Ningbo Road the next day. He took the money back to his hometown. The Chinese manager of the Qian Zhuang, Fu Xiang Qing, found out, reported it to the Hongkou police for arrest. The other day, Zhao A Qiao came to Shanghai from his hometown and hid in a house at No. 13 Dexing Lane, Haining Road. Hua Detective Zhang Shou Shan discovered this secretly and arrested him and took him to the police station. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the First Special Court's High Court. The police lawyer Zhang Tian Yin stated the previous situation and presented the check filled out by Zhao A Qiao. The manager of Qian Zhuang, Fu Xiang Qing, sent a representative to the court and reported the incident in detail. When questioned, the defendant admitted it without denial, saying that the check was written by someone surnamed Jia who set up a fortune-telling stall at the old garbage bridge. He hid 200 yuan of the money in his hometown and had already told the plaintiff to send someone to get it. He had used up 100 yuan. He threw the bankbook back into the accounting room from the window on the afternoon of the 17th of last month, etc., seeking consideration. Judge Shen Yun Rong ordered him to be remanded in custody for a later hearing.

Uniform Date for Changing Gas Station Licenses 199

Announcement by the Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau, Finance Bureau, and Public Works Bureau: In order to make an announcement, it is found that Article 16 of the Shanghai Municipal Regulations for the Management of Automobile Gas Stations states, "The business license of an automobile gas station shall be valid for a period of one year. Upon expiration, a new license shall be exchanged, and a license exchange fee of two silver dollars shall be paid." Furthermore, Article 17, Paragraph 3, states, "If the business license has expired and is still used without being exchanged, a fine of ten dollars shall be imposed, and a license shall still be exchanged." Therefore, the licenses of all automobile gas stations should be exchanged every year from the date of issuance. If the deadline is exceeded, a penalty will be imposed. However, because the issuance times are staggered, the exchange deadlines are not uniform. It is difficult for each station to remember, and the Bureau also finds it troublesome to issue them piecemeal and urge them separately. Therefore, we have followed the precedent of water pipe merchants and electrical material stores, reported to the Municipal Government, and uniformly set the exchange date. All automobile gas station licenses are changed to be issued between July 1st and July 31st of each year, which will be implemented from July 1st of this year. This is announced to the public. This announcement is made on June 9th, 21st year of the Republic of China, by Cai Zeng Ji, Director of the Finance Bureau, Jin Li Ren, Director of the Land Bureau, and Huang Bo Qiao, Director of the Public Works Bureau.

Conviction for Abuse of a Maid 200

The Maid is Returning to Her Hometown This Time

Huang Qian Huan, a native of Luoding County, Guangdong Province, with the courtesy name Chang Shu, used to work in the military department and has recently been unemployed. He brought his wife, Huang Tan, aged 24, and a maid, Pan Qin, aged 13, to live in Shanghai at No. 24 Guangtai Lai Hotel, Edouard Road, French Concession. Tan recently abused the maid, Pan Qin. On the 8th of this month, she used a chicken feather duster to severely beat the girl, causing bruises on her back, buttocks, and arms. The girl, unable to bear the suffering, stole 15 silver dollars when the Huang couple went out that evening, intending to take a boat back to her hometown alone. Because she did not know the way, she walked to the New Sun rooftop on Nanjing Road and was still wandering there at 12 o'clock that night. Patrolmen 893 and 779 of the Lao Zha Patrol Station found her and suspected her. They took her to the patrol station. After questioning by the patrol chief, because the incident occurred in the French Concession, they sent a detective to the French Patrol Station. After questioning by the patrol chief, Detective Ding Wen Sheng confirmed the facts and summoned Tan to the Second Special Court yesterday. Judge Zhang tried the case. Police lawyer Fei Xi Zhen stated the case, saying that the defendant's abuse of her granddaughter was obvious. The police prosecuted her under Article 293 of the Criminal Law and requested a trial. However, because the girl was beaten, she did not want to go back with the defendant and requested to be sent to the Tongxiang Association to be sent back to her hometown and handed over to her parents. The girl, Pan Qin, also testified that she was injured by the defendant. Tan, who is from Guangdong and does not speak the Shanghai dialect, was questioned and her husband came to court to testify on her behalf, saying that the girl did not do her job well and had stolen a wallet from a co-tenant the other day, so she was beaten. His wife found out and scolded and beat her. But the child is the daughter of a relative of my uncle and was given to me to adopt because her family was poor. It has been six years. Please hand her back. After verifying the confession in court, the court sentenced Huang Tan to a fine of 30 yuan for injuring someone, and if she was unable to pay the fine, she would be imprisoned for one day for every two yuan. The victim, Pan Qin, will be temporarily held at the patrol station and sent back to her hometown of Luoding County, Guangdong Province, by the Guangdong Tongxiang Association.

Soliciting Information on the Disappearance of Guo Qiu Sheng 201

Guo Qiu Sheng, a villager of the Wei family at No. 90 Dao Chuan Lane, West Gate, Shanghai, suddenly went missing on the morning of the 8th of this month at 7 a.m. Guo is 23 years old, from Tangxi Town, Hangxian County, Zhejiang Province. He is deaf and mute, has a shaved head, wears a small jacket and pants with white and blue stripes, is barefoot, wears broken black satin shoes, and wears an ebony ring on his hand. If anyone knows of his whereabouts, please contact the Wei family or the Red Cross on Second Avenue or the Shanghai County Government on Penglai Road in the city. There will be a reward.

Chang Shu De, a giant from Huaiyang, Henan Province, is 24 years old and over nine feet tall, taller than any giant who has come to Shanghai in the past. After the September 18th Incident, the National Games were suspended. The giant also became ill at Wuzhou Park due to acclimatization. After several months, he came to Shanghai recently and entered a hospital for treatment. It is said that after he recovers, he will travel to Europe and the United States with a certain Westerner.

Sincerely,

Nanjing Grand Theater

June 10, Year 21

To the esteemed editor of the Shen Bao newspaper:

According to the Shishi Xinbao newspaper, today's Shen Bao, Xinwen Bao, and Shibao all carried a news item titled "Aftermath of the Newspaper Workers' Strike Yesterday," along with a declaration from the Newspaper Workers' Union. The wording contains many inaccuracies.

On June 2nd, our newspaper's typesetting room was suddenly destroyed by thugs. One person, Zhang Zhuming, was arrested at the scene. After interrogation by the police, he confessed the names of his accomplices. In addition to He Zhaoxiong and three others, the rest are in hiding. On the 8th, it was discovered that these individuals were hiding in a house on Xiaotaoyuan Street in the Chinese area, still holding secret meetings and plotting to harm our newspaper.

To prevent any danger, our newspaper requested the Public Security Bureau to arrest and investigate them by name. In addition to arresting the defendants who jointly destroyed our newspaper's typesetting room, no damage was done to the equipment and miscellaneous items in the house. The statement in Shen Bao and other newspapers about the destruction of union equipment and miscellaneous items is fabricated and misleading. Moreover, those arrested are all co-defendants who harmed our newspaper, and there are confessions from the arrested defendants and witness testimonies on file. This is entirely a criminal matter and has nothing to do with the labor strike issue. Whether or not a crime is established will be determined by the court according to the law, which we will not elaborate on.

The news reported by Shen Bao and other newspapers is clearly inconsistent with the facts. We request that your lawyers send a letter to make a correction immediately.

Sincerely,

Lawyer Cha Renwei

Lawyer Zhang Zhengxue

June 10

To the esteemed editor of the Shen Bao newspaper:

I read in the newspaper yesterday about a Beijing dispatch stating that our lawyer was denied registration by the Ningbo Bar Association and cannot appear in court to defend Niu Lan. This case has been accepted by the High Court. Any lawyer registered with the High Court can appear in court, without being restricted by the designated district court area in the Lawyers' Regulations. Even if the case is tried in the Ningbo District Court in the future, it will still be considered a High Court case, not a District Court case. Therefore, since the prosecutor filed the lawsuit with the High Court, the High Court has also specially appointed a judge to go to Beijing to appear in court, which has nothing to do with the Ningbo Court. Our lawyer has been notified by the High Court to set a date and will go to review the files, indicating that there is no inability to perform his duties. The newspaper's report is likely based on inaccurate information.

We have received many inquiries from various circles and have not had time to answer them one by one. We kindly request that you publish this letter in your newspaper to correct the misunderstanding. We would be very grateful.

Sincerely,

Lawyer Chen Ying

Incoming Documents

Dong Xiujia's Draft

Jiangsu Province Three-Year Construction Plan (Continued) 213

Regarding highways, telecommunications, and provincial capital construction, the Jiangsu Provincial Highway Bureau was originally established to be responsible for the construction of provincial and county roads. The Jiangsu Provincial Telecommunications Management Office was originally established to be responsible for the management of electricity and telecommunications throughout the province. The Jiangsu Provincial Capital Construction Committee was originally established, later reduced to the Provincial Capital Construction Engineering Office, to be responsible for all construction in the provincial capital. In the winter of the 20th year, all of the above-mentioned original institutions were abolished and merged into this department for division management. The reason for the changes was to reduce government spending, and this consolidation was unavoidable. Although the difficulties in future progress were known, they could not be considered. The previous organizational structure of each bureau and office shared the responsibility of implementation, and this department only stood in a guiding and supervisory position. The current organizational structure places all implementation responsibilities in the supervisory body. Those who previously shared the work are now solely responsible. However, given the current financial constraints and tense situation, it is impossible to restore the original state. Since the responsibility lies with one body, all measures must be carried out diligently.

Now, regarding the completed projects of previous administrations, the projects that have been started but not completed, the projects that have been planned but not yet started, and the projects that have not been planned but still need to be designed, I dare to supplement them as much as possible within my ability and strive to complete the final three years of the tutelage period. Whether or not the goal can be achieved is uncertain, but I aim to work hard and advance bravely. All projects are divided by year and compiled separately later. Among them, water conservancy is particularly emphasized. Jiangsu Province is adjacent to the Yellow Sea to the east, connected to Huai, Mu, Yi, and Si to the north, and traversed by the Yangtze River in the middle. As for the Grand Canal, it connects to Shao, Bao, and Hongze lakes. More than twenty counties in Jiangbei turn into swamps whenever there is excessive rainfall. The sea dikes in Jiangnan are also of paramount importance. Last year's flood caused the simultaneous breach of the Grand Canal and sea dikes, resulting in countless injuries to people, farmlands, property, and livestock. Dikes everywhere were destroyed, which significantly impacted people's livelihoods. It is essential to know that to seek construction, people's livelihood must be the prerequisite. To solve the problem of people's livelihood, water conservancy must be revitalized. In this three-year plan, special attention is paid to water conservancy projects, which are listed as the top priority, followed by other projects. These projects will be carried out separately within these three years. Government officials will initiate at the front, and the public will assist at the rear. With everyone working together, success will be easy to achieve.

However, managing projects depends on sufficient funding. Jiangsu Province's special construction funds include road construction land tax, water conservancy land tax, special construction tax, and construction funds, totaling no less than three million yuan annually. At first glance, it may not seem small, but the actual annual revenue is often less than half of that. Examining the reasons, it may be due to reduced harvests, with surcharges decreasing along with the regular tax. Or it may be due to local financial difficulties, with construction funds being diverted for other purposes. Furthermore, the agencies responsible for collecting these special funds do not allocate them as they are collected, but rather accumulate them over time, making reform difficult. All of these factors have a significant impact on construction projects. Thorough rectification should be carried out in the future so that all facilities can be completed on schedule. Moreover, according to this plan, the various expenses cannot be met by a small number of special funds. It is essential to find new sources of income to achieve the desired effect.

Jiangsu Province has issued construction bonds to supplement the shortage of funds for various projects, with regular lotteries and a good reputation. The remaining face value is limited, but the annual project costs, based on the established plans, vary greatly. Therefore, it is necessary to continue issuing these bonds. As for the subsequent bond fund, it is proposed to collect from the beneficiaries or designate existing revenue to address the urgent needs, so that small amounts can be consolidated into a whole. This plan should still be carefully considered in conjunction with the competent financial authorities to avoid the disadvantages of harming the people and disturbing businesses while promoting construction. Moreover, there are benefits to promoting bonds for construction projects. For example, with the revitalization of water conservancy, disasters can be avoided, and harvests can be abundant. With the completion of highways, the networks will be connected, and transportation will be convenient. With the development of the telecommunications industry, all news can be transmitted quickly and without delay. With the prosperity of municipal administration, all facilities can be improved without being criticized for being simple. People can maximize their talents, land can maximize its benefits, things can maximize their use, and goods can flow smoothly. With the expansion of the effects of construction, the hopes of the people can be comforted, and the benefits of bonds will become apparent.

As for the standard for subsequent bond issuance, it will be based on the progress of the project, and the timely progress of the project depends on the bond funds as a very important foundation. Only then can this great construction be completed. Everything has rights and obligations. Purchasing bonds is an obligation, and rights are inherent in obligations. To seek the ultimate rights while avoiding the obligations beforehand is impossible. Therefore, construction bonds rely on the public's enthusiastic purchase, and government officials do their best to promote sales, working together for the future happiness of Jiangsu Province.

Furthermore, after the abolition of Likin duties, the associated construction revenue has been reduced by tens of thousands of yuan annually. Since Jiangsu Province has implemented a business tax to compensate for the lack of abolition, the construction sector should propose a percentage of the annual income to compensate for the removed surcharges. On one hand, the long-distance bus road maintenance fees for various roads should be reorganized, and the completed roads throughout the province should be opened to attract merchants to operate vehicles, thereby increasing the income from road maintenance fees. For the unfinished provincial and county roads, it is proposed to selectively contract merchants to build them and grant them the right to operate vehicles for a limited period. The above points take from the people for the benefit of the people, without being contradictory or involving excessive burden. As for the various minor surcharges, it is not appropriate to burden our people again. This is a brief summary of the financial aspects, presented at the end. It is hoped that the gentlemen of the country will understand together. I respectfully state the main points and hope for clear guidance.

"　言"

Positive and Negative 215

— Cimin

Below a horizontal line, there are the following two brief telegrams:

(1) "Songxia, accompanied by six or seven armed soldiers, met with ××× and questioned him about the External Affairs Ministry's protest against the Japanese army firing live ammunition in Yu and the bullet landing in the city. He also demanded × prove that the Japanese army did not fire live ammunition in Yu. × did not reply."

(2) "The vanguard of the Guizhou army entering Guangdong from Huaiji has reached the border of Guangning and Sihui. ××× ordered ××× to build an airfield in Beihai Dianbai to prepare to send aircraft to Nanlu. ×××'s unit, under the order of ×××, was transferred from Beijiang to the province and then to Nanlu; conscription has been extremely busy in the Guangsan Road area in recent days."

The first one is that the Japanese army asked a certain × to provide proof, but he did not reply. This is so secret and mysterious, as soft and elastic as cotton wool! The second one is strung together with words like Guizhou army...vanguard...prepare...send...

transfer...aircraft...conscription. This is so straightforward and obvious, as hard and decisive as pig iron!

The three words "did not reply" have erased so many facts. Is it "ignoring"? Or "tacitly agreeing"? Or "understanding"? I dare not speculate.

The actions of "sending...transferring...vanguard...conscription" are truly busy and tense. Is it "suppressing bandits"? Or "fighting our own people"? Or taking revenge on an "irreconcilable enemy"? I dare not guess.

But, within the same territory of our country, and both being military officers commanding troops, the performance is clearly one "negative" and one "positive". Who wouldn't believe it?

Someone might say, "Haven't you studied the materialistic dialectic of the times? This is called 'the unity of opposites'."

Literature and Art

Random Poems on the Shanghai Incident 216

— Songlu

The January 28th Incident, with people killed in the fields, blood flowing in the ditches, and the magnitude of the losses unprecedented, caused me to witness with a wounded heart, and grief and indignation had no outlet. I once wrote 30 poems to record the events. Now that the peace treaty has been signed, after the pain subsides, I feel even more emotional. I have extracted ten poems and submitted them to this publication to elicit sympathetic tears.

Without warning, the war clouds opened, and the sound of cannons roared like thunder all night. At dawn, putting on clothes, the crowd was shocked and asked, "Millions of elite troops have turned to ashes."

Outside the city of Liaoyang, corpses are still piled up, and on the banks of the Huangpu River, blood flows again. Before the great enemy, we must strive together, knowing that resistance to the enemy is our common cause.

Armored vehicles and cannons roamed day and night, and the Bao Tong Road was impassable. Generals fought bravely to die first, and one battle brought eternal fame.

Humiliatingly seeking peace is still unavoidable. How can we build meritorious achievements through bloody battles? One blow to the head frightens the Japanese, and the 19th Route Army is an iron army.

Science

Coloring Method on Copper and Ironware 217

— Liufang

Household odds and ends are mostly made of copper and iron, because they are cheap and durable, but they are prone to rust and unsightly. If we can use chemical methods and the power of medicines to achieve various beautiful colors, then although copper and iron are crude and cheap, their appearance will be no different from that of precious metals. Now I will describe the various dyeing methods in detail below.

Method for Dyeing Silver Color on Copperware

Two mace of mercury, one mace of alum powder, one mace of mercuric oxide.

Grind the above three ingredients into a powder. First, polish the copperware, then rub it vigorously with this mixed powder, and its color will be no different from silver.

Method for Dyeing Golden Color on Copperware

Three to four taels of potash (i.e., alkali), two taels and four qian of white alum.

Dissolve the above two ingredients in three pounds of clear water, put the copperware in, simmer until boiling, take it out, and then wash it very clean with this water. Then rub it with fine chalk powder, and it will appear as a bright golden yellow.

Method for Dyeing Black Color on Copperware

One part of tin nitrate, two parts of gold chloride.

First polish the copperware with chalk powder, then immerse it in the solution of the above two medicines. After a quarter of an hour, take it out and wipe it dry with a clean cloth, and it will become black copper.

Method for Dyeing Dark Green Color on Copperware

One part of ferric chloride, two parts of clear water.

First, polish the copperware and immerse it in the above solution. The color intensity depends on the duration of immersion.

Method for Dyeing Brown Color on Copperware

One tael of copper sulfate, one tael of zinc chloride, two taels of clear water.

First, polish the copperware, apply the above solution to the piece, and slowly bake it over a low fire until the piece is completely dry.

Method for Dyeing Silver Color on Ironware

Four taels and five qian of dragon's blood, six qian and three fen of arsenic trioxide powder, two taels and four qian of ammonium chloride.

Put the above three ingredients into a container with four pounds of 90-degree alcohol, add appropriate heat, and shake it frequently until it is completely dissolved. Then, polish the ironware and apply this medicinal solution to the piece. After it dries, there will be a thin layer of silver color on the surface, which is not only beautiful but also rustproof.

Method for Dyeing Golden Color on Ironware

Fourteen parts of manganese nitrate, six parts of pure alcohol.

First, polish the ironware and slightly heat it over a low fire. Then, dip a sponge in the above solution and apply it to the piece. Wait until it is dry and apply it again, repeating three or four times, and it will appear as a bright golden color.

Method for Dyeing Black Color on Ironware

Seven parts of copper nitrate, three parts of pure alcohol.

First, polish the ironware and slightly heat it over a low fire. Then, take a brush, dip it in the above solution, and apply it to the piece. After cooling, a black copper oxide film will form on the piece. Peel it off by hand, and a carbon-colored substance will remain on the inner surface of the piece. Repeat this process several times, and it will become a glossy black metalware.

Method for Dyeing Brown Color on Ironware

Eight parts of ferric chloride, four parts of antimony chloride, two parts of tannic acid, eight parts of clear water.

First, polish, wash, and dry the ironware. Then, dip a sponge in the above solution and apply it to the piece, rubbing it vigorously. The color intensity depends on the number of times the solution is applied. When the color is appropriate, let it sit for a while, wash it clean with clear water, dry it, and then apply linseed oil to the piece.

Method for Dyeing Carbon Color on Ironware

One point and six fen of ammonium sulfite, six parts of clear water.

First, dye the ironware according to the procedure for dyeing golden color, then immerse it in the above solution and repeat it again and again until the desired color is obtained.

Business Economics

Please Call a Doctor 218

— Iwano

Mr. Li's little treasure, Xiong'er, was lively and smiling at lunchtime, but for some reason, he suddenly started crying and fussing two hours after the meal, unable to sit or lie down properly. His wife quickly called her husband back from school to discuss what to do.

When Mr. Li returned and saw Xiong'er's condition and felt his forehead and body, which were burning hot, he knew that the illness had come suddenly. His wife said, "Quickly call Dr. So-and-so to see him, don't hesitate, or the illness will worsen."

Mr. Li frowned and said, "Dr. So-and-so? He is indeed an expert in pediatrics, but it is afternoon now, and he only sees patients in the morning. The people said, "Then hurry up and ask him to come." Mr. Li said, "Ask him to come? We can't afford it, a house call costs eight yuan and eight jiao! Do we have that much money?" Mrs. Li was so anxious that she shed tears and said, "Dr. Wang in the front alley, I heard that he will come to see a patient anytime you ask him, as long as it is one yuan. Let's ask him to take a look first." Although Mr. Li did not want to delay with a mediocre doctor, he felt his pocket, and where would he get eight yuan and eight jiao? He had to listen to his wife and go to the front alley to invite Dr. Wang. As he went, he kept saying in his mouth, "The poor are sick, it is not good to be sick in the afternoon!"

After taking a dose of Dr. Wang's medicine, Xiong'er's condition not only did not improve but showed significant progress. They did not close their eyes all night. Xiong'er was uncomfortable, and they were even more uncomfortable in their hearts. At eight o'clock in the morning, they hurriedly took Xiong'er to the pediatrics expert. Who knew that many people had already arrived first? Mr. Li hurriedly took out one yuan and two jiao to register, but it was already number nineteen. He went to the examination room to take a look, but the doctor had not yet arrived. He saw that the clock had struck nine, and thought that the diagnosis would begin, but the doctor did not enter the examination room but went out and sat in a rickshaw. When he asked those who had registered, they said, "This is an early house call, someone invited him for eight yuan and eight jiao. The clinic here stipulates that it will not start until ten o'clock." When Mr. Li heard this, he could not help but repeat "eight yuan eight, eight yuan eight."

At ten o'clock, the diagnosis began, starting with number one. When it got to number eight, Mr. and Mrs. Li rejoiced, thinking that Xiong'er would be next in another hour. Just as they were watching number nine pass, suddenly number ten was skipped and a new arrival was seen. Mr. Li was about to ask why he did not follow the order and came from behind, when he suddenly thought that this was called "pulling the number," and that he had paid double the consultation fee to enjoy this priority. So he could not help but call out "two yuan four, two yuan four."

When it got to number eighteen, just as number eighteen stood up from the stool next to the doctor, Mr. Li hugged Xiong'er and wanted to go up to take his place when suddenly there was another "pull the number," another two yuan four jiao causing mischief and driving him aside. Mr. Li stood aside, worried that another two yuan four would come, but fortunately, this "pull the number" was pulled away, and it was his Xiong'er's turn. He was registered as number nineteen, but in fact, he was number twenty-one, and he could not return until 13:00 after arriving at 8:30.

On the way back, he patted Xiong'er and said, "Baby, it's not good to get sick in the future. If you get sick, don't get sick in the afternoon, because it costs eight yuan eight jiao!" And he gently patted him and said, "If you unfortunately get sick and go there, don't encounter 'pulling the number,' we can't 'pull,' because 'pulling' costs two yuan four jiao!"

Heaven and Earth

Each Generation is Worse Than the Last 219

— Shou

I often hear many people say that the more civilized humans become, the more they use their brains, so the lifespan of humans is getting shorter. From one point of view, it is certainly correct, but the general facts are not so. Look at the people in various countries around the world, they do not have shorter lifespans because of the progress of civilization, but rather they are getting younger and healthier as they get older. For example, Edison used his brain more severely than the average person, but he did not have a shorter lifespan because of it. Because they can see this danger, they pay twelve points of attention to eugenics and physical education, so that each body can develop a strong foundation, and then they bravely go forward to do it. Even if we take the people of the same race in Japan as an example, they have been able to keep pace with Europe and the United States and pay attention to this danger. Look at the newly formed cabinet in Japan this time, the oldest member is seventy-nine years old and the youngest is forty-nine years old. The average is almost sixty years old. People like this in their twilight years can still shoulder the heavy responsibility of the country and prepare to do something. How surprising is this kind of physique and spirit to us? But in the mouths of the Chinese, it is "Old but not dead, called a thief."

On the other hand, the people in the country are not like that. In the past fifty years, they have also learned some superficial civilization, but they have also used their brains a lot, but unfortunately they have used them in the wrong way, specializing in selfishness and benefiting themselves at the expense of others. At the same time, they do not pay attention to eugenics and physical education, resulting in a group of sickly young people. May I ask whether this kind of people can live long, whether they can have the courage to move forward. As for the elderly, once they are over fifty years old, they do not want to continue working, and they retire into the forest. This is called "enjoying happiness." Even if you want to do it, people will say that you are old and mediocre and have entered the ranks of being overthrown. Therefore, I often hear the older generation say, "Each generation is worse than the last!"

Jiangsu Higher Court Second Branch 221

Civil Judgment: Xu Shouzhen versus Cai Wenhua regarding a lawsuit for the return of funds (Main Text): The appeal and the appellee's application for provisional execution are both rejected. The appellant bears the second instance litigation costs. ▲ Kang Long Yanghang versus Hefeng Hao regarding a lawsuit over an order (Main Text): The original judgment is changed. The appellee shall compensate the appellant five hundred taels of silver. The remainder of the appeal is rejected. The appellee bears the first and second instance litigation costs.

Civil Ruling: Xu Zhongyi versus Wang Xikun regarding a lawsuit over a deposit (Main Text): The appeal is rejected. The appellant bears the second instance litigation costs. ▲ Kaiqing Nuoweisigan et al. versus Aosilandanda regarding a lawsuit over debt, application for restoration to original condition and appeal (Main Text): The appeal is rejected. The appellant bears the appeal costs.

Song Zhizhou and Cheng Weixin are sentenced to two years and six months of imprisonment for crudely organizing a group with the aim of endangering the Republic of China. The number of days of detention before the judgment becomes final shall be deducted from the imprisonment term at a rate of two days for one day. Documents containing reactionary meaning are confiscated. Wang Yangshi, Wang Yuhua, and Huang Zhuren are all found not guilty. ▲ Zhu Youwen et al. regarding an appeal for robbery (Main Text): The original judgment is revoked. Zhu Youwen is sentenced to ten years of imprisonment for joint robbery. Xu Asheng, as a repeat offender for joint robbery, is sentenced to fourteen years of imprisonment. One handgun and five bullets are confiscated. ▲ Dong Manni regarding a case of endangering the Republic of China (Main Text): Xun Manni is found not guilty. Leaflets and books containing reactionary meaning are confiscated.
